/// with integer element type.    unsigned BitSize = getSizeInBits();\n      return BitSize >= 8 && !(BitSize & (BitSize - 1));\n    }\n\n    /// Return true if this has the same number of bits as VT.\n    bool bitsEq(EVT VT) const than VT.\n    bool knownBitsLT(EVT VT) const {\n      return TypeSize::isKnownLT(getSizeInBits(), VT.getSizeInBits());\n    }\n\n    /// Return true if we know at compile time this has fewer than or assert(isScalableVector() == VT.isScalableVector() &&\n             \"Comparison between scalable and fixed types\");\n      return knownBitsGE(VT);\n    }\n\n    /// Return true if this has less bits than VT.\n    bool bitsLT(EVT VT) const {\n      if (EVT::operator==(VT)) return false;\n      assert(isScalableVector() == VT.isScalableVector() &&\n             \"Comparison between scalable and assert(isScalableVector() == VT.isScalableVector() &&\n             \"Comparison between scalable and fixed types\");\n      return knownBitsLE(VT);\n    }\n\n    /// Return the SimpleValueType held in the specified simple EVT.\n    MVT getSimpleVT() const {\n      assert(isSimple() && \"Expected a SimpleValueType!\");\n      return V;\n    }\n\n    /// If this is a vector type, return the getExtendedVectorElementType();\n    }\n\n    /// Given a vector type, return the number of elements it contains.\n    unsigned getVectorNumElements() const {\n      assert(isVector() && \"Invalid vector type!\");\n\n      if (isScalableVector())\n        llvm::reportFatalInternalError(\n            \"Possible incorrect use of EVT::getVectorNumElements() for \"\n            \"scalable vector. Scalable flag may be dropped, use \"\n            \"EVT::getVectorElementCount() instead\");\n\n      return isSimple() ? V.getVectorNumElements()\n                        : getExtendedVectorNumElements();\n    }\n\n    // Given a (possibly scalable) vector type, return the ElementCount\n    ElementCount getVectorElementCount() const {\n      assert((isVector()) && \"Invalid vector type!\");\n      if (isSimple())\n        return V.getVectorElementCount();\n\n      return getExtendedVectorElementCount();\n    }\n\n    /// Given a vector type, return the minimum number of elements it contains.\n    unsigned getVectorMinNumElements() const {\n      return getVectorElementCount().getKnownMinValue();\n    }\n\n    /// Given a RISCV vector tuple type, return the num_fields.\n    unsigned getRISCVVectorTupleNumFields() const {\n      return V.getRISCVVectorTupleNumFields();\n    }\n\n    /// Return the size of the specified value type in bits.\n    ///\n    /// If the value type is a scalable vector type, the scalable property will\n    /// be set and the runtime size will be a positive integer multiple of the\n    /// base size.\n    TypeSize getSizeInBits() const {\n      if (isSimple())\n        return V.getSizeInBits();\n      return getExtendedSizeInBits();\n    }\n\n    /// Return the size of the specified fixed width value type in bits. The\n    /// function will assert if the type is scalable.\n    uint64_t getFixedSizeInBits() const {\n      return getSizeInBits().getFixedValue();\n    }\n\n    uint64_t getScalarSizeInBits() const {\n      return getScalarType().getSizeInBits().getFixedValue();\n    }\n\n    /// Return the number of bytes overwritten by a store of the specified value\n    /// type.\n    ///\n    /// If the value type is a scalable vector type, the scalable property will\n    /// be set and the runtime size will be a positive integer multiple of the\n    /// base size.\n    TypeSize getStoreSize() const {\n      TypeSize BaseSize = getSizeInBits();\n      return {(BaseSize.getKnownMinValue() + 7) / 8, BaseSize.isScalable()};\n    }\n\n    // Return the number of bytes overwritten by a store of this value type or\n    // this value type's element type in the case of a vector.\n    uint64_t getScalarStoreSize() const {\n      return getScalarType().getStoreSize().getFixedValue();\n    }\n\n    /// Return the number of bits overwritten by a store of the specified value\n    /// type.\n    ///\n    /// If the value type is a scalable vector type, the scalable property will\n    /// be set and the runtime size will be a positive integer multiple of the\n    /// base size.\n    TypeSize getStoreSizeInBits() const {\n      return getStoreSize() * 8;\n    }\n\n    /// Rounds the bit-width of the given integer EVT up to the nearest power of\n    /// two (and at least to eight), and returns the integer EVT with that\n    /// number of bits.\n    EVT getRoundIntegerType(LLVMContext &Context) const {\n      assert(isInteger() && !isVector() && \"Invalid integer type!\");\n      unsigned BitWidth = getSizeInBits();\n      if (BitWidth <= 8)\n        return EVT(MVT::i8);\n      return getIntegerVT(Context, llvm::bit_ceil(BitWidth));\n    }\n\n    /// Finds the smallest simple value type that is greater than or equal to\n    /// half the width of this EVT. If no simple value type can be found, an\n    /// extended integer value type of half the size (rounded up) is returned.\n    EVT getHalfSizedIntegerVT(LLVMContext &Context) const {\n      assert(isInteger() && !isVector() && \"Invalid integer type!\");\n      unsigned EVTSize = getSizeInBits();\n      for (unsigned IntVT = MVT::FIRST_INTEGER_VALUETYPE;\n          IntVT <= MVT::LAST_INTEGER_VALUETYPE; ++IntVT) {\n        EVT HalfVT = EVT((MVT::SimpleValueType)IntVT);\n        if (HalfVT.getSizeInBits() * 2 >= EVTSize)\n          return HalfVT;\n      }\n      return getIntegerVT(Context, (EVTSize + 1) / 2);\n    }\n\n    /// Return a VT for an integer vector type with the size of the\n    /// elements doubled. The typed returned may be an extended type.\n    EVT widenIntegerVectorElementType(LLVMContext &Context) const {\n      EVT EltVT = getVectorElementType();\n      EltVT = EVT::getIntegerVT(Context, 2 * EltVT.getSizeInBits());\n      return EVT::getVectorVT(Context, EltVT, getVectorElementCount());\n    }\n\n    // Return a VT for a vector type with the same element type but\n    // half the number of elements. The type returned may be an\n    // extended type.\n    EVT getHalfNumVectorElementsVT(LLVMContext &Context) const {\n      EVT EltVT = getVectorElementType();\n      auto EltCnt = getVectorElementCount();\n      assert(EltCnt.isKnownEven() && \"Splitting vector, but not in half!\");\n      return EVT::getVectorVT(Context, EltVT, EltCnt.divideCoefficientBy(2));\n    }\n\n    // Return a VT for a vector type with the same element type but\n    // double the number of elements. The type returned may be an\n    // extended type.\n    EVT getDoubleNumVectorElementsVT(LLVMContext &Context) const {\n      EVT EltVT = getVectorElementType();\n      auto EltCnt = getVectorElementCount();\n      return EVT::getVectorVT(Context, EltVT, EltCnt * 2);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns true if the given vector is a power of 2.\n    bool isPow2VectorType() const {\n      unsigned NElts = getVectorMinNumElements();\n      return !(NElts & (NElts - 1));\n    }\n\n    /// Widens the length of the given vector EVT up to the nearest power of 2\n    /// and returns that type.\n    EVT getPow2VectorType(LLVMContext &Context) const {\n      if (!isPow2VectorType()) {\n        ElementCount NElts = getVectorElementCount();\n        unsigned NewMinCount = 1 << Log2_32_Ceil(NElts.getKnownMinValue());\n        NElts = ElementCount::get(NewMinCount, NElts.isScalable());\n        return EVT::getVectorVT(Context, getVectorElementType(), NElts);\n      }\n      else {\n        return *this;\n      }\n    }\n\n    /// This function returns value type as a string, e.g. \"i32\".\n    LLVM_ABI std::string getEVTString() const;\n\n    /// Support for debugging, callable in GDB: VT.dump()\n    LLVM_ABI void dump() const;\n\n    /// Implement operator<<.\n    void print(raw_ostream &OS) const {\n      OS << getEVTString();\n    }\n\n    /// This method returns an LLVM type corresponding to the specified EVT.\n    /// For integer types, this returns an unsigned type. Note that this will\n    /// abort for types that cannot be represented.\n    LLVM_ABI Type *getTypeForEVT(LLVMContext &Context) const;\n\n    /// Return the value type corresponding to the specified type.\n    /// If HandleUnknown is true, unknown types are returned as Other,\n    /// otherwise they are invalid.\n    /// NB: This includes pointer types, which require a DataLayout to convert\n    /// to a concrete value type.\n    LLVM_ABI static EVT getEVT(Type *Ty, bool HandleUnknown = false);\n\n    intptr_t getRawBits() const {\n      if (isSimple())\n        return V.SimpleTy;\n      else\n        return (intptr_t)(LLVMTy);\n    }\n\n    /// A meaningless but well-behaved order, useful for constructing\n    /// containers.\n    struct compareRawBits {\n      bool operator()(EVT L, EVT R) const {\n        if (L.V.SimpleTy == R.V.SimpleTy)\n          return L.LLVMTy < R.LLVMTy;\n        else\n          return L.V.SimpleTy < R.V.SimpleTy;\n      }\n    };\n\n    /// Returns an APFloat semantics tag appropriate for the value type. If this\n    /// is a vector type, the element semantics are returned.\n    LLVM_ABI const fltSemantics &getFltSemantics() const;\n\n  private:\n    // Methods for handling the Extended-type case in functions above.\n    // These are all out-of-line to prevent users of this header file\n    // from having a dependency on Type.h.\n    LLVM_ABI EVT changeExtendedTypeToInteger() const;\n    LLVM_ABI EVT changeExtendedVectorElementType(EVT EltVT) const;\n    LLVM_ABI EVT changeExtendedVectorElementTypeToInteger() const;\n    LLVM_ABI static EVT getExtendedIntegerVT(LLVMContext &C, unsigned BitWidth);\n    LLVM_ABI static EVT getExtendedVectorVT(LLVMContext &C, EVT VT,\n                                            unsigned NumElements,\n                                            bool IsScalable);\n    LLVM_ABI static EVT getExtendedVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT,\n                                            ElementCount EC);\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtendedFloatingPoint() const LLVM_READONLY;\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtendedInteger() const LLVM_READONLY;\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtendedScalarInteger() const LLVM_READONLY;\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtendedVector() const LLVM_READONLY;\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtended16BitVector() const LLVM_READONLY;\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtended32BitVector() const LLVM_READONLY;\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtended64BitVector() const LLVM_READONLY;\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtended128BitVector() const LLVM_READONLY;\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtended256BitVector() const LLVM_READONLY;\n    LLVM_ABI bool isExtended512BitVector() const {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_0111TnSu5wKGDxRq5H3H298V","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→//===-- LegalizeTypes.cpp - Common code for DAG type legalizer ------------===//\n     2→//\n     3→// Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\n     4→// See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\n     5→// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\n     6→//\n     7→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n     8→//\n     9→// This file implements the SelectionDAG::LegalizeTypes method.  It transforms\n    10→// an arbitrary well-formed SelectionDAG to only consist of legal types.  This\n    11→// is common code shared among the LegalizeTypes*.cpp files.\n    12→//\n    13→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    14→\n    15→#include \"LegalizeTypes.h\"\n    16→#include \"llvm/ADT/SetVector.h\"\n    17→#include \"llvm/IR/DataLayout.h\"\n    18→#include \"llvm/Support/CommandLine.h\"\n    19→#include \"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\"\n    20→#include \"llvm/Support/raw_ostream.h\"\n    21→using namespace llvm;\n    22→\n    23→#define DEBUG_TYPE \"legalize-types\"\n    24→\n    25→static cl::opt<bool>\n    26→EnableExpensiveChecks(\"enable-legalize-types-checking\", cl::Hidden);\n    27→\n    28→/// Do extensive, expensive, basic correctness checking.\n    29→void DAGTypeLegalizer::PerformExpensiveChecks() {\n    30→  // If a node is not processed, then none of its values should be mapped by any\n    31→  // of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n    32→\n    33→  // If a node is processed, then each value with an illegal type must be mapped\n    34→  // by exactly one of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n    35→  // Values with a legal type may be mapped by ReplacedValues, but not by any of\n    36→  // the other maps.\n    37→\n    38→  // Note that these invariants may not hold momentarily when processing a node:\n    39→  // the node being processed may be put in a map before being marked Processed.\n    40→\n    41→  // Note that it is possible to have nodes marked NewNode in the DAG.  This can\n    42→  // occur in two ways.  Firstly, a node may be created during legalization but\n    43→  // never passed to the legalization core.  This is usually due to the implicit\n    44→  // folding that occurs when using the DAG.getNode operators.  Secondly, a new\n    45→  // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\n    46→  // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\n    47→  // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis.  Whether\n    48→  // it actually morphs or not depends on whether, after updating its operands,\n    49→  // it is equivalent to an existing node: if so, it morphs into that existing\n    50→  // node (CSE).  An operand can change during analysis if the operand is a new\n    51→  // node that morphs, or it is a processed value that was mapped to some other\n    52→  // value (as recorded in ReplacedValues) in which case the operand is turned\n    53→  // into that other value.  If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\n    54→  // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\n    55→  // to live on in the DAG.\n    56→  // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\n    57→  // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\n    58→  // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\n    59→  // not used by them.\n    60→\n    61→  // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\n    62→  // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\n    63→\n    64→  // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\n    65→  // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\n    66→\n    67→  // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\n    68→  // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes). It transforms\n// an arbitrary well-formed SelectionDAG to only consist of legal types.  This\n// is common code shared among the LegalizeTypes*.cpp files.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#include \"LegalizeTypes.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/SetVector.h\"\n#include \"llvm/IR/DataLayout.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/CommandLine.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/raw_ostream.h\"\nusing namespace llvm;\n\n#define DEBUG_TYPE \"legalize-types\"\n\nstatic cl::opt<bool>\nEnableExpensiveChecks(\"enable-legalize-types-checking\", cl::Hidden);\n\n/// Do extensive, expensive, basic correctness checking.\nvoid DAGTypeLegalizer::PerformExpensiveChecks() {\n  // If a node is not processed, then none of its values should be mapped by any\n  // of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n\n  // If a node is processed, then each value with an illegal type must be mapped\n  // by exactly one of PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, ..., ReplacedValues.\n  // Values with a legal type may be mapped by ReplacedValues, but not by any of\n  // the other maps.\n\n  // Note that these invariants may not hold momentarily when processing a node:\n  // the node being processed may be put in a map before being marked Processed.\n\n  // Note that it is possible to have nodes marked NewNode in the DAG.  This can\n  // occur in two ways.  Firstly, a node may be created during legalization but\n  // never passed to the legalization core.  This is usually due to the implicit\n  // folding that occurs when using the DAG.getNode operators.  Secondly, a new\n  // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\n  // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\n  // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis.  Whether\n  // it actually morphs or not depends on whether, after updating its operands,\n  // it is equivalent to an existing node: if so, it morphs into that existing\n  // node (CSE).  An operand can change during analysis if the operand is a new\n  // node that morphs, or it is a processed value that was mapped to some other\n  // value (as recorded in ReplacedValues) in which case the operand is turned\n  // into that other value.  If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\n  // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\n  // to live on in the DAG.\n  // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\n  // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\n  // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\n  // not used by them.\n\n  // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\n  // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\n\n  // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\n  // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\n\n  // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\n  // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes).  This means that it may\n  // also map nodes marked NewNode if the deallocated memory was reallocated as\n  // another node, and that new node was not seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery\n  // (for example because it was created but not used).  In general, we cannot\n  // distinguish between new nodes and deleted nodes.\n  SmallVector<SDNode*, 16> NewNodes;\n  for (SDNode &Node : DAG.allnodes()) {\n    // Remember nodes marked NewNode - they are subject to extra checking below.\n    if (Node.getNodeId() == NewNode)\n      NewNodes.push_back(&Node);\n\n    for (unsigned i = 0, e = Node.getNumValues(); i != e; ++i) {\n      SDValue Res(&Node, i);\n      bool Failed = false;\n      // Don't create a value in map.\n      auto ResId = ValueToIdMap.lookup(Res);\n\n      unsigned Mapped = 0;\n      if (ResId) {\n        auto I = ReplacedValues.find(ResId);\n        if (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n          Mapped |= 1;\n          // Check that remapped values are only used by nodes marked NewNode.\n          for (SDUse &U : Node.uses())\n            if (U.getResNo() == i)\n              assert(U.getUser()->getNodeId() == NewNode &&\n                     \"Remapped value has non-trivial use!\");\n\n          // Check that the final result of applying ReplacedValues is not\n          // marked NewNode.\n          auto NewValId = I->second;\n          I = ReplacedValues.find(NewValId);\n          while (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n            NewValId = I->second;\n            I = ReplacedValues.find(NewValId);\n          }\n          SDValue NewVal = getSDValue(NewValId);\n          (void)NewVal;\n          assert(NewVal.getNode()->getNodeId() != NewNode &&\n                 \"ReplacedValues maps to a new node!\");\n        }\n        if (PromotedIntegers.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 2;\n        if (SoftenedFloats.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 4;\n        if (ScalarizedVectors.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 8;\n        if (ExpandedIntegers.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 16;\n        if (ExpandedFloats.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 32;\n        if (SplitVectors.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 64;\n        if (WidenedVectors.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 128;\n        if (PromotedFloats.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 256;\n        if (SoftPromotedHalfs.count(ResId))\n          Mapped |= 512;\n      }\n\n      if (Node.getNodeId() != Processed) {\n        // Since we allow ReplacedValues to map deleted nodes, it may map nodes\n        // marked NewNode too, since a deleted node may have been reallocated as\n        // another node that has not been seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery.\n        if ((Node.getNodeId() == NewNode && Mapped > 1) ||\n            (Node.getNodeId() != NewNode && Mapped != 0)) {\n          dbgs() << \"Unprocessed value in a map!\";\n          Failed = true;\n        }\n      } else if (isTypeLegal(Res.getValueType()) || IgnoreNodeResults(&Node)) {\n        if (Mapped > 1) {\n          dbgs() << \"Value with legal type was transformed!\";\n          Failed = true;\n        }\n      } else {\n        if (Mapped == 0) {\n          SDValue NodeById = IdToValueMap.lookup(ResId);\n          // It is possible the node has been remapped to another node and had\n          // its Id updated in the Value to Id table. The node it remapped to\n          // may not have been processed yet. Look up the Id in the Id to Value\n          // table and re-check the Processed state. If the node hasn't been\n          // remapped we'll get the same state as we got earlier.\n          if (NodeById->getNodeId() == Processed) {\n            dbgs() << \"Processed value not in any map!\";\n            Failed = true;\n          }\n        } else if (Mapped & (Mapped - 1)) {\n          dbgs() << \"Value in multiple maps!\";\n          Failed = true;\n        }\n      }\n\n      if (Failed) {\n        if (Mapped & 1)\n          dbgs() << \" ReplacedValues\";\n        if (Mapped & 2)\n          dbgs() << \" PromotedIntegers\";\n        if (Mapped & 4)\n          dbgs() << \" SoftenedFloats\";\n        if (Mapped & 8)\n          dbgs() << \" ScalarizedVectors\";\n        if (Mapped & 16)\n          dbgs() << \" ExpandedIntegers\";\n        if (Mapped & 32)\n          dbgs() << \" ExpandedFloats\";\n        if (Mapped & 64)\n          dbgs() << \" SplitVectors\";\n        if (Mapped & 128)\n          dbgs() << \" WidenedVectors\";\n        if (Mapped & 256)\n          dbgs() << \" PromotedFloats\";\n        if (Mapped & 512)\n          dbgs() << \" SoftPromoteHalfs\";\n        dbgs() << \"\\n\";\n        llvm_unreachable(nullptr);\n      }\n    }\n  }\n\n#ifndef NDEBUG\n  // Checked that NewNodes are only used by other NewNodes.\n  for (SDNode *N : NewNodes) {\n    for (SDNode *U : N->users())\n      assert(U->getNodeId() == NewNode && \"NewNode used by non-NewNode!\");\n  }\n#endif\n}\n\n/// This is the main entry point for the type legalizer. Check to see if any operands are new,\n    // and if so, mark them. Implicit folding by the DAG.getNode operators and\n  // node morphing can cause unreachable nodes to be around with their flags set\n  // to new.\n  DAG.RemoveDeadNodes();\n\n  // In a debug build, scan all the nodes to make sure we found them all.  This\n  // ensures that there are no cycles and that everything got processed.\n#ifndef NDEBUG\n  for (SDNode &Node : DAG.allnodes()) {\n    bool Failed = false;\n\n    // Check that all result types are legal.\n    if (!IgnoreNodeResults(&Node))\n      for (unsigned i = 0, NumVals = Node.getNumValues(); i < NumVals; ++i)\n        if (!isTypeLegal(Node.getValueType(i))) {\n          dbgs() << \"Result type \" << i << \" illegal: \";\n          Node.dump(&DAG);\n          Failed = true;\n        }\n\n    // Check that all operand types are legal.\n    for (unsigned i = 0, NumOps = Node.getNumOperands(); i < NumOps; ++i)\n      if (!IgnoreNodeResults(Node.getOperand(i).getNode()) &&\n          !isTypeLegal(Node.getOperand(i).getValueType())) {\n        dbgs() << \"Operand type \" << i << \" illegal: \";\n        Node.getOperand(i).dump(&DAG);\n        Failed = true;\n      }\n\n    if (Node.getNodeId() != Processed) {\n       if (Node.getNodeId() == NewNode)\n         dbgs() << \"New node not analyzed?\\n\";\n       else if (Node.getNodeId() == Unanalyzed)\n         dbgs() << \"Unanalyzed node not noticed?\\n\";\n       else if (Node.getNodeId() > 0)\n         dbgs() << \"Operand not processed?\\n\";\n       else if (Node.getNodeId() == ReadyToProcess)\n         dbgs() << \"Not added to worklist?\\n\";\n       Failed = true;\n    }\n\n    if (Failed) {\n      Node.dump(&DAG); dbgs() << \"\\n\";\n      llvm_unreachable(nullptr);\n    }\n  }\n#endif\n\n  return Changed;\n}\n\n/// The specified node is the root of a subtree of potentially new nodes.\n/// Correct any processed operands (this may change the node) and calculate the\n/// NodeId. The depth of this walk is bounded by the size\n  // of the new tree that was constructed (usually 2-3 nodes), so we don't worry\n  // about revisiting of nodes.\n  //\n  // As we walk the operands, keep track of the number of nodes that are\n  // processed.  If non-zero, this will become the new nodeid of this node.\n  // Operands may morph when they are analyzed.  If so, the node will be\n  // updated after all operands have been analyzed.  Since this is rare,\n  // the code tries to minimize overhead in the non-morphing case.\n\n  std::vector<SDValue> NewOps;\n  unsigned NumProcessed = 0;\n  for (unsigned i = 0, e = N->getNumOperands(); i != e; ++i) {\n    SDValue OrigOp = N->getOperand(i);\n    SDValue Op = OrigOp;\n\n    AnalyzeNewValue(Op); // Op may morph.\n\n    if (Op.getNode()->getNodeId() == Processed)\n      ++NumProcessed;\n\n    if (!NewOps.empty()) {\n      // Some previous operand changed.  Add this one to the list.\n      NewOps.push_back(Op);\n    } else if (Op != OrigOp) {\n      // This is the first operand to change - add all operands so far.\n      llvm::append_range(NewOps, N->ops().take_front(i));\n      NewOps.push_back(Op);\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Some operands changed - update the node.\n  if (!NewOps.empty()) {\n    SDNode *M = DAG.UpdateNodeOperands(N, NewOps);\n    if (M != N) {\n      // The node morphed into a different node.  Normally for this to happen\n      // the original node would have to be marked NewNode.  However this can\n      // in theory momentarily not be the case while ReplaceValueWith is doing\n      // its stuff.  Mark the original node NewNode to help basic correctness\n      // checking.\n      N->setNodeId(NewNode);\n      if (M->getNodeId() != NewNode && M->getNodeId() != Unanalyzed)\n        // It morphed into a previously analyzed node - nothing more to do.\n        return M;\n\n      // It morphed into a different new node.  Do the equivalent of passing\n      // it to AnalyzeNewNode: expunge it and calculate the NodeId.  No need\n      // to remap the operands, since they are the same as the operands we\n      // remapped above.\n      N = M;\n    }\n  }\n\n  // Calculate the NodeId.\n  N->setNodeId(N->getNumOperands() - NumProcessed);\n  if (N->getNodeId() == ReadyToProcess)\n    Worklist.push_back(N);\n\n  return N;\n}\n\n/// Call AnalyzeNewNode, updating the node in Val if needed.\n/// If the node changes to a processed node, then remap it.\nvoid DAGTypeLegalizer::AnalyzeNewValue(SDValue &Val) {\n  Val.setNode(AnalyzeNewNode(Val.getNode()));\n  if (Val.getNode()->getNodeId() == Processed)\n    // We were passed a processed node, or it morphed into one - remap it.\n    RemapValue(Val);\n}\n\n/// If the specified value was already legalized to another value,\n/// replace it by that value.\nvoid DAGTypeLegalizer::RemapValue(SDValue &V) {\n  auto Id = getTableId(V);\n  V = getSDValue(Id);\n}\n\nvoid DAGTypeLegalizer::RemapId(TableId &Id) {\n  auto I = ReplacedValues.find(Id);\n  if (I != ReplacedValues.end()) {\n    assert(Id != I->second && \"Id is mapped to itself.\");\n    // Use path compression to speed up future lookups if values get multiply\n    // replaced with other values.\n    RemapId(I->second);\n    Id = I->second;\n\n    // Note that N = IdToValueMap[Id] it is possible to have\n    // N.getNode()->getNodeId() == NewNode at this point because it is possible\n    // for a node to be put in the map before being processed.\n  }\n}\n\nnamespace {\n  /// This class is a DAGUpdateListener that listens for updates to nodes and\n  /// recomputes their ready state.\n  class NodeUpdateListener : public SelectionDAG::DAGUpdateListener {\n    DAGTypeLegalizer &DTL;\n    SmallSetVector<SDNode*, 16> &NodesToAnalyze;\n  public:\n    explicit NodeUpdateListener(DAGTypeLegalizer &dtl,\n                                SmallSetVector<SDNode*, 16> &nta)","numLines":400,"startLine":200,"totalLines":1048}}}

This is a private interface\n    10→// shared between the code that implements the SelectionDAG::LegalizeTypes\n    11→// method.\n    12→//\n    13→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    14→\n    15→#ifndef LLVM_LIB_CODEGEN_SELECTIONDAG_LEGALIZETYPES_H\n    16→#define LLVM_LIB_CODEGEN_SELECTIONDAG_LEGALIZETYPES_H\n    17→\n    18→#include \"MatchContext.h\"\n    19→#include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n    20→#include \"llvm/CodeGen/SelectionDAG.h\"\n    21→#include \"llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h\"\n    22→#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n    23→\n    24→namespace llvm {\n    25→\n    26→//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    27→/// This takes an arbitrary SelectionDAG as input and hacks on it until only\n    28→/// value types the target machine can handle are left. This involves promoting\n    29→/// small sizes to large sizes or splitting up large values into small values.\n    30→///\n    31→class LLVM_LIBRARY_VISIBILITY DAGTypeLegalizer {\n    32→  const TargetLowering &TLI;\n    33→  SelectionDAG &DAG;\n    34→public:\n    35→  /// This pass uses the NodeId on the SDNodes to hold information about the\n    36→  /// state of the node. The enum has all the values.\n    37→  enum NodeIdFlags {\n    38→    /// All operands have been processed, so this node is ready to be handled.\n    39→    ReadyToProcess = 0,\n    40→\n    41→    /// This is a new node, not before seen, that was created in the process of\n    42→    /// legalizing some other node.\n    43→    NewNode = -1,\n    44→\n    45→    /// This node's ID needs to be set to the number of its unprocessed\n    46→    /// operands.\n    47→    Unanalyzed = -2,\n    48→\n    49→    /// This is a node that has already been processed.\n    50→    Processed = -3\n    51→\n    52→    // 1+ - This is a node which has this many unprocessed operands.\n    53→  };\n    54→private:\n    55→\n    56→  /// This is a bitvector that contains two bits for each simple value type,\n    57→  /// where the two bits correspond to the LegalizeAction enum from\n    58→  /// TargetLowering. This can be queried with \"getTypeAction(VT)\".\n    59→  TargetLowering::ValueTypeActionImpl ValueTypeActions;\n    60→\n    61→  /// Return how we should legalize values of this type.\n    62→  TargetLowering::LegalizeTypeAction getTypeAction(EVT VT) const {\n    63→    return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT);\n    64→  }\n    65→\n    66→  /// Return true if this type is legal on this target.\n    67→  bool isTypeLegal(EVT VT) const {\n    68→    return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT) == TargetLowering::TypeLegal;\n    69→  }\n    70→\n    71→  /// Return true if this is a simple legal type.\n    72→  bool isSimpleLegalType(EVT VT) const {\n    73→    return VT.isSimple() && TLI.isTypeLegal(VT);\n    74→  }\n    75→\n    76→  EVT getSetCCResultType(EVT VT) const {\n    77→    return TLI.getSetCCResultType(DAG.getDataLayout(), *DAG.getContext(), VT);\n    78→  }\n    79→\n    80→  /// Pretend all of this node's results are legal.\n    81→  bool IgnoreNodeResults(SDNode *N) const {\n    82→    return N->getOpcode() == ISD::TargetConstant ||\n    83→           N->getOpcode() == ISD::Register;\n    84→  }\n    85→\n    86→  // Bijection from SDValue to unique id. As each created node gets a\n    87→  // new id we do not need to worry about reuse expunging.  Should we\n    88→  // run out of ids, we can do a one time expensive compactifcation.\n    89→  typedef unsigned TableId;\n    90→\n    91→  TableId NextValueId = 1;\n    92→\n    93→  SmallDenseMap<SDValue, TableId, 8> ValueToIdMap;\n    94→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, SDValue, 8> IdToValueMap;\n    95→\n    96→  /// For integer nodes that are below legal width, this map indicates what\n    97→  /// promoted value to use.\n    98→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> PromotedIntegers;\n    99→\n   100→  /// For integer nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which\n   101→  /// operands are the expanded version of the input.\n   102→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> ExpandedIntegers;\n   103→\n   104→  /// For floating-point nodes converted to integers of the same size, this map\n   105→  /// indicates the converted value to use.\n   106→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> SoftenedFloats;\n   107→\n   108→  /// For floating-point nodes that have a smaller precision than the smallest\n   109→  /// supported precision, this map indicates what promoted value to use.\n   110→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> PromotedFloats;\n   111→\n   112→  /// For floating-point nodes that have a smaller precision than the smallest\n   113→  /// supported precision, this map indicates the converted value to use.\n   114→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> SoftPromotedHalfs;\n   115→\n   116→  /// For float nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which operands\n   117→  /// are the expanded version of the input.\n   118→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> ExpandedFloats;\n   119→\n   120→  /// For nodes that are <1 x ty>, this map indicates the scalar value of type\n   121→  /// 'ty' to use.\n   122→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> ScalarizedVectors;\n   123→\n   124→  /// For nodes that need to be split this map indicates which operands are the\n   125→  /// expanded version of the input.\n   126→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> SplitVectors;\n   127→\n   128→  /// For vector nodes that need to be widened, indicates the widened value to\n   129→  /// use.\n   130→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> WidenedVectors;\n   131→\n   132→  /// For values that have been replaced with another, indicates the replacement\n   133→  /// value to use.\n   134→  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> ReplacedValues;\n   135→\n   136→  /// This defines a worklist of nodes to process. In order to be pushed onto\n   137→  /// this worklist, all operands of a node must have already been processed.\n   138→  SmallVector<SDNode*, 128> Worklist;\n   139→\n   140→  TableId getTableId(SDValue V) {\n   141→    assert(V.getNode() && \"Getting TableId on SDValue()\");\n   142→\n   143→    auto I = ValueToIdMap.find(V);\n   144→    if (I != ValueToIdMap.end()) {\n   145→      // replace if there's been a shift.\n   146→      RemapId(I->second);\n   147→      assert(I->second && \"All Ids should be nonzero\");\n   148→      return I->second;\n   149→    }\n   150→    // Add if it's not there.\n   151→    ValueToIdMap.insert(std::make_pair(V, NextValueId));\n   152→    IdToValueMap.insert(std::make_pair(NextValueId, V));\n   153→    ++NextValueId;\n   154→    assert(NextValueId != 0 &&\n   155→           \"Ran out of Ids. Increase id type size or add compactification\");\n   156→    return NextValueId - 1;\n   157→  }\n   158→\n   159→  const SDValue &getSDValue(TableId &Id) {\n   160→    RemapId(Id);\n   161→    assert(Id && \"TableId should be non-zero\");\n   162→    auto I = IdToValueMap.find(Id);\n   163→    assert(I != IdToValueMap.end() && \"cannot find Id in map\");\n   164→    return I->second;\n   165→  }\n   166→\n   167→public:\n   168→  explicit DAGTypeLegalizer(SelectionDAG &dag)\n   169→    : TLI(dag.getTargetLoweringInfo()), DAG(dag),\n   170→    ValueTypeActions(TLI.getValueTypeActions()) {\n   171→  }\n   172→\n   173→  /// This is the main entry point for the type legalizer. This is a private interface\n// shared between the code that implements the SelectionDAG::LegalizeTypes\n// method.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_LIB_CODEGEN_SELECTIONDAG_LEGALIZETYPES_H\n#define LLVM_LIB_CODEGEN_SELECTIONDAG_LEGALIZETYPES_H\n\n#include \"MatchContext.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n#include \"llvm/CodeGen/SelectionDAG.h\"\n#include \"llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n/// This takes an arbitrary SelectionDAG as input and hacks on it until only\n/// value types the target machine can handle are left. This involves promoting\n/// small sizes to large sizes or splitting up large values into small values.\n///\nclass LLVM_LIBRARY_VISIBILITY DAGTypeLegalizer {\n  const TargetLowering &TLI;\n  SelectionDAG &DAG;\npublic:\n  /// This pass uses the NodeId on the SDNodes to hold information about the\n  /// state of the node. The enum has all the values.\n  enum NodeIdFlags {\n    /// All operands have been processed, so this node is ready to be handled.\n    ReadyToProcess = 0,\n\n    /// This is a new node, not before seen, that was created in the process of\n    /// legalizing some other node.\n    NewNode = -1,\n\n    /// This node's ID needs to be set to the number of its unprocessed\n    /// operands.\n    Unanalyzed = -2,\n\n    /// This is a node that has already been processed.\n    Processed = -3\n\n    // 1+ - This is a node which has this many unprocessed operands.\n  };\nprivate:\n\n  /// This is a bitvector that contains two bits for each simple value type,\n  /// where the two bits correspond to the LegalizeAction enum from\n  /// TargetLowering. This can be queried with \"getTypeAction(VT)\".\n  TargetLowering::ValueTypeActionImpl ValueTypeActions;\n\n  /// Return how we should legalize values of this type.\n  TargetLowering::LegalizeTypeAction getTypeAction(EVT VT) const {\n    return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT);\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this type is legal on this target.\n  bool isTypeLegal(EVT VT) const {\n    return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT) == TargetLowering::TypeLegal;\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a simple legal type.\n  bool isSimpleLegalType(EVT VT) const {\n    return VT.isSimple() && TLI.isTypeLegal(VT);\n  }\n\n  EVT getSetCCResultType(EVT VT) const {\n    return TLI.getSetCCResultType(DAG.getDataLayout(), *DAG.getContext(), VT);\n  }\n\n  /// Pretend all of this node's results are legal.\n  bool IgnoreNodeResults(SDNode *N) const {\n    return N->getOpcode() == ISD::TargetConstant ||\n           N->getOpcode() == ISD::Register;\n  }\n\n  // Bijection from SDValue to unique id. As each created node gets a\n  // new id we do not need to worry about reuse expunging.  Should we\n  // run out of ids, we can do a one time expensive compactifcation.\n  typedef unsigned TableId;\n\n  TableId NextValueId = 1;\n\n  SmallDenseMap<SDValue, TableId, 8> ValueToIdMap;\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, SDValue, 8> IdToValueMap;\n\n  /// For integer nodes that are below legal width, this map indicates what\n  /// promoted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> PromotedIntegers;\n\n  /// For integer nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which\n  /// operands are the expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> ExpandedIntegers;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes converted to integers of the same size, this map\n  /// indicates the converted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> SoftenedFloats;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes that have a smaller precision than the smallest\n  /// supported precision, this map indicates what promoted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> PromotedFloats;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes that have a smaller precision than the smallest\n  /// supported precision, this map indicates the converted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> SoftPromotedHalfs;\n\n  /// For float nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which operands\n  /// are the expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> ExpandedFloats;\n\n  /// For nodes that are <1 x ty>, this map indicates the scalar value of type\n  /// 'ty' to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> ScalarizedVectors;\n\n  /// For nodes that need to be split this map indicates which operands are the\n  /// expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> SplitVectors;\n\n  /// For vector nodes that need to be widened, indicates the widened value to\n  /// use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> WidenedVectors;\n\n  /// For values that have been replaced with another, indicates the replacement\n  /// value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> ReplacedValues;\n\n  /// This defines a worklist of nodes to process. In order to be pushed onto\n  /// this worklist, all operands of a node must have already been processed.\n  SmallVector<SDNode*, 128> Worklist;\n\n  TableId getTableId(SDValue V) {\n    assert(V.getNode() && \"Getting TableId on SDValue()\");\n\n    auto I = ValueToIdMap.find(V);\n    if (I != ValueToIdMap.end()) {\n      // replace if there's been a shift.\n      RemapId(I->second);\n      assert(I->second && \"All Ids should be nonzero\");\n      return I->second;\n    }\n    // Add if it's not there.\n    ValueToIdMap.insert(std::make_pair(V, NextValueId));\n    IdToValueMap.insert(std::make_pair(NextValueId, V));\n    ++NextValueId;\n    assert(NextValueId != 0 &&\n           \"Ran out of Ids. Increase id type size or add compactification\");\n    return NextValueId - 1;\n  }\n\n  const SDValue &getSDValue(TableId &Id) {\n    RemapId(Id);\n    assert(Id && \"TableId should be non-zero\");\n    auto I = IdToValueMap.find(Id);\n    assert(I != IdToValueMap.end() && \"cannot find Id in map\");\n    return I->second;\n  }\n\npublic:\n  explicit DAGTypeLegalizer(SelectionDAG &dag)\n    : TLI(dag.getTargetLoweringInfo()), DAG(dag),\n    ValueTypeActions(TLI.getValueTypeActions()) {\n  }\n\n  /// This is the main entry point for the type legalizer.  This does a\n  /// top-down traversal of the dag, legalizing types as it goes.  Returns\n  /// \"true\" if it made any changes.\n  bool run();\n\n  void NoteDeletion(SDNode *Old, SDNode *New) {\n    assert(Old != New && \"node replaced with self\");\n    for (unsigned i = 0, e = Old->getNumValues(); i != e; ++i) {\n      TableId NewId = getTableId(SDValue(New, i));\n      TableId OldId = getTableId(SDValue(Old, i));\n\n      if (OldId != NewId) {\n        ReplacedValues[OldId] = NewId;\n\n        // Delete Node from tables.  We cannot do this when OldId == NewId,\n        // because NewId can still have table references to it in\n        // ReplacedValues.\n        IdToValueMap.erase(OldId);\n        PromotedIntegers.erase(OldId);\n        ExpandedIntegers.erase(OldId);\n        SoftenedFloats.erase(OldId);\n        PromotedFloats.erase(OldId);\n        SoftPromotedHalfs.erase(OldId);\n        ExpandedFloats.erase(OldId);\n        ScalarizedVectors.erase(OldId);\n        SplitVectors.erase(OldId);\n        WidenedVectors.erase(OldId);\n      }\n\n      ValueToIdMap.erase(SDValue(Old, i));\n    }\n  }\n\n  SelectionDAG &getDAG() const { return DAG; }\n\nprivate:\n  SDNode *AnalyzeNewNode(SDNode *N);\n  void AnalyzeNewValue(SDValue &Val);\n  void PerformExpensiveChecks();\n  void RemapId(TableId &Id);\n  void RemapValue(SDValue &V);\n\n  // Common routines.\n  SDValue BitConvertToInteger(SDValue Op);\n  SDValue BitConvertVectorToIntegerVector(SDValue Op);\n  SDValue CreateStackStoreLoad(SDValue Op, EVT DestVT);\n  bool CustomLowerNode(SDNode *N, EVT VT, bool LegalizeResult);\n  bool CustomWidenLowerNode(SDNode *N, EVT VT);\n\n  /// Replace each result of the given MERGE_VALUES node with the corresponding\n  /// input operand, except for the result 'ResNo', for which the corresponding\n  /// input operand is returned.\n  SDValue DisintegrateMERGE_VALUES(SDNode *N, unsigned ResNo);\n\n  SDValue JoinIntegers(SDValue Lo, SDValue Hi);\n\n  std::pair<SDValue, SDValue> ExpandAtomic(SDNode *Node);\n\n  SDValue PromoteTargetBoolean(SDValue Bool, EVT ValVT);\n\n  void ReplaceValueWith(SDValue From, SDValue To);\n  void SplitInteger(SDValue Op, SDValue &Lo, SDValue &Hi);\n  void SplitInteger(SDValue Op, EVT LoVT, EVT HiVT,\n                    SDValue &Lo, SDValue &Hi);\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Integer Promotion Support: LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n  /// Given a processed operand Op which was promoted to a larger integer type,\n  /// this returns the promoted value. The low bits of the promoted value\n  /// corresponding to the original type are exactly equal to Op.\n  /// The extra bits contain rubbish, so the promoted value may need to be zero-\n  /// or sign-extended from the original type before it is usable (the helpers\n  /// SExtPromotedInteger and ZExtPromotedInteger can do this for you).\n  /// For example, if Op is an i16 and was promoted to an i32, then this method\n  /// returns an i32, the lower 16 bits of which coincide with Op, and the upper\n  /// 16 bits of which contain rubbish.\n  SDValue GetPromotedInteger(SDValue Op) {\n    TableId &PromotedId = PromotedIntegers[getTableId(Op)];\n    SDValue PromotedOp = getSDValue(PromotedId);\n    assert(PromotedOp.getNode() && \"Operand wasn't promoted?\");\n    return PromotedOp;\n  }\n  void SetPromotedInteger(SDValue Op, SDValue Result);\n\n  /// Get a promoted operand and sign extend it to the final size.\n  SDValue SExtPromotedInteger(SDValue Op) {\n    EVT OldVT = Op.getValueType();\n    SDLoc dl(Op);\n    Op = GetPromotedInteger(Op);\n    return DAG.getNode(ISD::SIGN_EXTEND_INREG, dl, Op.getValueType(), Op,\n                       DAG.getValueType(OldVT));\n  }\n\n  /// Get a promoted operand and zero extend it to the final size.\n  SDValue ZExtPromotedInteger(SDValue Op) {\n    EVT OldVT = Op.getValueType();\n    SDLoc dl(Op);\n    Op = GetPromotedInteger(Op);\n    return DAG.getZeroExtendInReg(Op, dl, OldVT);\n  }\n\n  // Promote the given operand V (vector or scalar) according to N's specific\n  // reduction kind. N must be an integer VECREDUCE_* or VP_REDUCE_*. Returns\n  // the nominal extension opcode (ISD::(ANY|ZERO|SIGN)_EXTEND) and the\n  // promoted value.\n  SDValue PromoteIntOpVectorReduction(SDNode *N, SDValue V);\n\n  // Integer Result Promotion.\n  void PromoteIntegerResult(SDNode *N, unsigned ResNo);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_MERGE_VALUES(SDNode *N, unsigned ResNo);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_AssertSext(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_AssertZext(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_Atomic0(AtomicSDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_Atomic1(AtomicSDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_AtomicCmpSwap(AtomicSDNode *N, unsigned ResNo);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_EXTRACT_SUBVECTOR(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_INSERT_SUBVECTOR(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_VECTOR_REVERSE(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_VECTOR_SHUFFLE(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_VECTOR_SPLICE(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_VECTOR_INTERLEAVE_DEINTERLEAVE(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_BUILD_VECTOR(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_ScalarOp(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_STEP_VECTOR(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_EXTEND_VECTOR_INREG(SDNode *N);\n  SDValue PromoteIntRes_INSERT_VECTOR_ELT(SDNode *N);","numLines":300,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1229}}}
